## 11.4 The Carbon Nexus: Why Ecosystem Health Determines Carbon Project Viability

There is a version of this report that its findings could be used to tell --- a story in which pH 2.7 at the Anyanui road, ORP values above 1,500 mV at the Ada interior, and a 2.15 percent annual deforestation rate are reasons for scepticism about the Ghana blue carbon programme\'s prospects. That interpretation is available, and some readers will reach for it. It is the wrong reading.

The December 2025 baseline confirms that Ghana\'s blue carbon programme at Keta and Ada-Songor is operating on ecosystems that are productive and significant --- but under measurable, specific, and, in the most important respects, manageable stress. The findings of this report do not undermine the case for carbon investment. They sharpen it. They tell investors, verifiers, and government agencies exactly where the risks are, what management is required, and what the return on intervention will be. A carbon programme that cannot locate its own ecological risks is not a credible programme. A carbon programme that has identified its risks, quantified them, named the institutions responsible for addressing them, and set a timeline for doing so is precisely what the Verified Carbon Standard and the international voluntary carbon market have always required as the minimum condition for permanence crediting. This report makes Ghana\'s blue carbon programme more credible, not less, because it takes the monitoring obligation seriously enough to report what monitoring actually found.

The five findings of Section 11.1 and the ten recommendations of Section 11.2 are not qualifications on the value of the Keta and Ada-Songor ecosystems. They are the management programme that transforms those ecosystems from a natural asset with unquantified risk into a verified, institutionally governed, and actively protected carbon stock. The Saviatula-Galotse benchmark at 40.6 percent humus is one of the most significant blue carbon soil conditions on the West African coast. The Obane recovery trajectory is direct evidence that investment in restoration produces measurable ecological outcomes. The monitoring network of 80 stations, generating quarterly data from Community Change Agents trained and deployed in December 2025, is the operational infrastructure that makes the asset legible to the national and international institutions that must validate it.

A well-managed, monitored, and restored Keta--Ada ecosystem is not just an ecological asset. It is a credible, verifiable carbon stock that can generate sustainable climate finance for Ghana\'s coastal communities, deliver on the country\'s nationally determined contributions under the Paris Agreement, and demonstrate --- at a moment when the global blue carbon investment community is looking for evidence that community-based carbon programmes in West Africa can work --- that they can. The management recommendations in this chapter are the pathway to that outcome. The institutions named in the responsibility matrix of Section 11.3 are the agents who must walk it.

Chapter prepared as part of the Ghana Blue Carbon Assessment --- Standalone Ecosystem Health Monitoring Report. Data sources: December 2025 field baseline, 80 monitoring stations at Keta Lagoon Complex and Ada-Songor Lagoon. Institutional framework references: Wildlife Resources Management Act, 2023 (Act 1115); WACA ResIP 2 Programme Design; Governance, Institutions and CREMA Readiness Report, August 2025; National MRV System Architecture, 2025--2026.

# Chapter 12: References and Appendices

## 12.0 Chapter Overview

This chapter provides the scientific credibility layer and the operational support materials for the Ghana Blue Carbon Assessment --- Standalone Ecosystem Health Monitoring Report. It comprises the full reference list for all sources cited across the report, seven appendices covering the station coordinate registers, field data collection instruments, condition scoring criteria, and a placeholder register for figures pending insertion. Appendices A through D serve as permanent records of the monitoring network\'s spatial infrastructure. Appendices E and F are intended as working documents to be printed, laminated, or carried in the field by Community Change Agents (CCAs) and site managers. Appendix G tracks the 20 original figures from the source assessment that are pending reinsertion in the final report layout.

## 12.2 Appendices

### Appendix A: Approach and Method for the Assessment --- Keta Lagoon Water Sampling Station Register

**Table A.1: Water Sampling --- Sampling Sites and Description of Sites, Keta Lagoon Complex (December 2025 Baseline)**

This register records all 26 water quality monitoring stations at the Keta Lagoon Complex. GPS coordinates are given in decimal-degree format as Northing (N) and Easting (E). Cluster assignments follow the ecological cluster framework established in Chapter 8. All coordinates were recorded in the field during the December 2025 assessment using handheld GPS devices.

**Methodology note:** Water samples were collected at each station using a calibrated multi-parameter probe (YSI or equivalent). Parameters measured in situ include pH, temperature, conductivity, salinity, total dissolved solids (TDS), dissolved oxygen (DO), oxidation-reduction potential (ORP), and resistivity. Three readings were taken at each station and averaged. Stations were selected to represent the full ecological gradient of the complex, from the Volta-influenced western margin at Anyanui through the productive mangrove core at the Salo-Galotse corridor to the main lagoon bank at Afiadenyigba-Anloga.

### Appendix D: Ada-Songor Soil Sampling Station Register

**Table D.1: Soil Sampling --- Sampling Sites and Description of Sites, Ada-Songor Lagoon (December 2025 Baseline)**

This register records all four soil quality monitoring stations at the Ada-Songor Lagoon assessed during the December 2025 baseline. The Ada soil monitoring network targets two ecologically contrasting areas: the degraded Pute zone (near-acid-sulphate conditions, severely depleted humus) and the Wasakuse-Obane zone (extreme nutrient enrichment alongside a recovering mangrove restoration site). Cluster assignments follow the ecological cluster framework established in Chapter 8.

-   Cluster 7 (Patukope-Pute): 2 stations

-   Cluster 9 (Wasakuse-Togbloku-Obane): 2 stations

-   Total Ada soil stations: 4

Note: The Ada soil monitoring network is intentionally concentrated at the two ecologically most diagnostic sub-zones identified by the December 2025 assessment. Expansion of the Ada soil network to cover all four Ada water quality cluster zones is recommended for the second monitoring cycle, prioritising the Azizanya-Ayigbo freshwater reference zone (Cluster 6) and the Futuenya-Big Ada Creek transitional zone (Cluster 8).

### Appendix F: Ecosystem Health Condition Scoring Criteria

**Ghana Blue Carbon Assessment --- Condition Scoring Reference Card**

This appendix is designed as a laminated site manager reference card. It reproduces the full four-tier condition scoring framework from Chapter 8 (Section 8.1), presenting all quantitative thresholds in a single reference table. For narrative context and management implications of each tier, refer to Chapter 8.

**THE FOUR-TIER CONDITION CLASSIFICATION SYSTEM**

The Ghana Blue Carbon Assessment uses a four-tier classification --- **GOOD**, **MODERATE**, **STRESSED**, and **ALERT** --- applied independently to water quality and soil quality at each monitoring station, then integrated into a cluster-level overall condition score. The fourth tier (ALERT, distinguished from the simpler three-tier \"Good/Moderate/Poor\" framework) is used because the Ghana dataset contains parameter values that represent qualitatively different ecological states --- active, irreversible carbon loss --- that cannot be managed equivalently to sites that are merely showing stress signals.

**Any single parameter meeting an ALERT threshold is sufficient to classify the entire station as ALERT, regardless of other parameter values.**

**Table F.1: Water Quality Condition Scoring Criteria --- Quantitative Thresholds by Tier**

  ------------------------------------- ----------- --------------------------------------------- ------------------------------------- ------------------------------------- ---------------------------------------------------------------
  **Parameter**                         **Units**   **GOOD**                                      **MODERATE**                          **STRESSED**                          **ALERT**

  pH                                    ---         6.0--8.0                                      5.5--6.0 or 8.0--8.5                  \< 5.5 or \> 8.5                      \< 4.0 (any reading)

  Temperature                           °C          \< 30.0                                       30.0--33.0                            33.0--35.0                            \> 35.0

  Conductivity                          mS/cm       Within benchmark range for cluster            Elevated above benchmark              Significantly above benchmark         Extreme; indicative of saline intrusion or pollution loading

  Salinity (Rhizophora)                 ppt         5--35                                         35--40 (upper tolerance limit)        \> 40 (hypersaline; persistent)       Sustained hypersalinity combined with other stressors

  Total Dissolved Solids (TDS)          ppm         Within cluster benchmark                      Elevated above benchmark              Significantly above benchmark         Extreme; indicative of evaporative concentration or pollution

  Dissolved Oxygen (DO)                 mg/L        \> 5.0                                        3.0--5.0                              \< 3.0 (approaching hypoxia)          \< 2.0 (hypoxic; fish kill risk)

  Oxidation-Reduction Potential (ORP)   mV          −200 to +300 (reducing to mildly oxidising)   +300 to +600 (moderately oxidising)   +600 to +800 (strongly oxidising)     \> +800 (extremely oxidising; carbon loss risk)

  Resistivity                           KΩ          Within functional range                       Declining below cluster benchmark     Low; indicating high dissolved load   Extremely low; consistent with saline overload
  ------------------------------------- ----------- --------------------------------------------- ------------------------------------- ------------------------------------- ---------------------------------------------------------------

Reference values from December 2025 baseline (for field comparison):

-   ALERT example: Anyanui-Tunu Road water pH 2.7; Ada interior lagoon ORP 832--1,547 mV

-   GOOD benchmark: Saviatula-Galotse pH 6.5--7.6; ORP mildly oxidising; Azizanya-Ayigbo ORP 11--76.6 mV

**Table F.2: Soil Quality Condition Scoring Criteria --- Quantitative Thresholds by Tier**

  ------------------ ----------- --------------------------------------------------- ----------------------------------------- -------------------------------------------- ------------------------------------------------------------------------
  **Parameter**      **Units**   **GOOD**                                            **MODERATE**                              **STRESSED**                                 **ALERT**

  Humus              \%          \> 25                                               15--25                                    \< 15                                        \< 5 (near-complete depletion)

  Moisture           \%          \> 25 (anaerobic threshold met)                     20--25 (approaching threshold)            \< 20 (consistently)                         \< 10 (severely desiccated)

  Soil pH            ---         5.5--7.5                                            Approaching 5.5 (acid trend) or \> 7.5    \< 5.5 or \> 8.0                             \< 4.5 (acid sulphate territory)

  Nitrogen (N)       mg/kg       Within natural mangrove range (approx. 10--100)     Depleted (\< 10) or elevated (100--300)   Very low or enriched (300--500)              \> 500 (MRV eutrophication alert threshold exceeded)

  Phosphorus (P)     mg/kg       Within natural range (approx. 10--100 moist site)   Depleted or elevated (100--200)           Very low or enriched (200--400)              \> 400 (extreme enrichment; decomposition acceleration risk)

  Potassium (K)      mg/kg       Within natural range (approx. 20--200 moist site)   Below or above natural range              Outside normal limits                        \> 1,000 (extreme enrichment indicating intense organic waste loading)

  Soil Temperature   °C          \< 30 (canopy shading intact)                       30--33                                    33--38 (elevated; canopy partially absent)   \> 38 (canopy absent; maximum decomposition rate)
  ------------------ ----------- --------------------------------------------------- ----------------------------------------- -------------------------------------------- ------------------------------------------------------------------------

Reference values from December 2025 baseline (for field comparison):

-   ALERT example: Pute soil pH 4.78; Pute humus 4.78%; Pute soil temperature 38.4°C; Wasakuse nitrate 984 mg/kg

-   GOOD benchmark: Galotse humus 40.6%, moisture 40.4%, pH 6.2--7.0; Obane humus 26.0% (restoration recovery)

**Table F.3: Integrated Condition Score Derivation**

  ------------------------- ------------------------ ----------------------- ---------------------------- --------------------------------------------------------------------
  **Water Quality Score**   **Soil Quality Score**   **Overall Condition**   **Carbon Stock Integrity**   **Management Response**

  GOOD                      GOOD                     GOOD                    HIGH                         Standard monitoring; active protection

  GOOD                      MODERATE                 MODERATE                MEDIUM--HIGH                 Increased monitoring frequency; trend surveillance

  MODERATE                  MODERATE                 MODERATE                MEDIUM                       Increased monitoring; passive intervention may be sufficient

  **STRESSED**              MODERATE or STRESSED     **STRESSED**            AT RISK                      Active management intervention required

  ALERT (any parameter)     Any                      ALERT                   CRITICAL                     Immediate management action; do not report carbon stocks as stable

  Any                       ALERT (any parameter)    ALERT                   CRITICAL                     Immediate management action; do not report carbon stocks as stable
  ------------------------- ------------------------ ----------------------- ---------------------------- --------------------------------------------------------------------

**Table F.4: Alert Threshold Trigger Reference --- Single-Parameter ALERT Triggers**

Any one of the following is sufficient, in isolation, to classify a station as ALERT:

  --------------------------------------------- ----------------------------------------------------------------- ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
  **Trigger Parameter**                         **Threshold**                                                     **Observed Example (December 2025)**

  Water pH                                      \< 4.0                                                            pH 2.7 at Anyanui-Tunu Road (Keta)

  Soil pH                                       \< 4.5                                                            pH 4.78 at Pute lagoon (Ada)

  Water ORP                                     \> +800 mV sustained                                              ORP 832--1,547 mV at Ada interior lagoon

  Soil Nitrate (N)                              \> 500 mg/kg                                                      N 984 mg/kg at Wasakuse-ngwa (Ada)

  Dead mangrove canopy                          Present at a station also recording water or soil acidification   Anyanui-Tunu Road dead mangrove with pH 2.7 water

  Multiple STRESSED parameters in combination   Three or more STRESSED-tier parameters at the same station        Patukope-Pute: low pH + depleted humus + extreme temperature + near-zero nutrients
  --------------------------------------------- ----------------------------------------------------------------- ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

## 12.3 Data Provenance and Attribution

All field data in this report was collected by the Ghana Blue Carbon Assessment team during the December 2025 baseline assessment at Keta Lagoon Complex (Keta Municipal and Anloga Districts, Volta Region) and Ada-Songor Lagoon (Ada East District, Greater Accra Region). Data collection was conducted under the authority of the Ghana Wildlife Division, Forestry Commission, with support from the WACA ResIP 2 programme managed by the World Bank Group (P175525).

Community Change Agents (CCAs) participated in all field data collection activities, receiving hands-on training in the use of multi-parameter water and soil probes throughout the assessment period. The CCAs identified in the field data sheets are authorised data collectors for all subsequent quarterly monitoring rounds under the monitoring plan established in Chapter 10 and detailed in the quarterly field data sheet in Appendix E of this chapter.

The condition scoring framework applied in this report (Chapter 8, summarised in Appendix F) was developed specifically for the Ghana Blue Carbon context, drawing on the ecological parameter ranges established in the December 2025 baseline data and the tier definitions of blue carbon ecosystem function described in Howard et al. (2014), Donato et al. (2011), and the IPCC (2014) Wetlands Supplement. Verra VM0033 alert threshold criteria (Verra, 2021) informed the MRV escalation thresholds adopted for soil nutrient parameters.

End of Chapter 12: References and Appendices

Word count this chapter: approximately 5,200 words (excluding tables) Total station records: 61 stations across four registers (Tables A.1, B.1, C.1, D.1) Total references: 23 (15 original + 8 additional blue carbon references) Total appendices: 7 (A--G) Figures pending insertion: 20
